      "title": "UNDEFINED",
      "body": " Your friend Susan has become interested in functions \\(f\\colon\\R \\sto \\R\\) which preserve both the operation of addition and the operation of multiplication; that is, functions \\(f\\) which satisfy  \\begin{align}           f(x+y) \u0026\u003d f(x) + f(y)     \\\\ \\intertext{and}           f(xy)  \u0026\u003d f(x)f(y)    \\end{align} for all \\(x,y \\in \\R.\\)   Naturally she started her investigation by looking at some examples. After expending considerable effort she was unable to find additional examples.    She now conjectures that there are no other functions satisfying \\eqref{pf_30_1} and\\eqref{pf_30_2}.   Write Susan a letter explaining why she is correct.   \u003ci\u003eHint.\u003c/i\u003e  You may choose to pursue the following line of argument. After expending considerable effort she was unable to find additional examples.    She now conjectures that there are no other functions satisfying \\eqref{pf_30_1} and\\eqref{pf_30_2}. [In \\eqref{pf_30_1} let \\(y\u003d0\\).]\n  (b) Show that if \\(a \\ne 0\\) and \\(a \u003d ab\\), then \\(b\u003d1\\).\n  (c) Show that \\(f(1) \u003d 1\\). [Write \\(x\\) as \\(\\sqrt x\\sqrt x\\) and use\\eqref{pf_30_2}.]\n  (i) Show that if \\(x \\le y\\), then \\(f(x) \\le f(y)\\).
